0374214913|3.0|Penumbra has a great setup, and the author is obviously a talented \\"idea guy\\" (in silicon valley speak). The first third of the book draws you into its mystery in the same way that the titular bookstore draws in its special brand of late night visitors. Sloan's rich descriptions of places and objects make you want to visit the store, climb through the vertical stacks, and touch crumbly leather-bound volumes. The premise is familiar, but no less welcome: ordinary people, secrets hidden in plain view and amongst everyday objects, the hidden fantastical underbelly of the mundane. It's hard not to love the sort of magic realism that's teased here.<br /><br />But, as with many books cemented in the fantasy genre, meaningful character development is all but missing. Characters often come off as one dimensional, arc-less, and in some cases, downright annoying. For example, the character of Kat, who seems to have been created just to provide a fill-in-the-blank love interest with geek cred, allowing the author to name drop far too many silicon valley buzzwords in an attempt to seem modern and relevant to a young adult audience. Valley startup culture is worshiped in this book like no other fiction that I've ever read or ever want to read again, and the overuse of tech terminology borders on the embarrassing. Ever watched an episode of NCIS where a \\"hacker\\" rattles off a string of unintelligible words that are all real things, but that don't quite make sense in the given context? That'll be a familiar sensation here. Yes, Ruby is a programming language. No, a neophyte would not use it to make a 3D model of a bookstore in an evening. Yes, I'm the guy that has to point that out. Sorry. Sometimes I post comments on Youtube too.<br /><br />As others have pointed out, Penumbra's ending is a bit rushed and sloppy, though I actually liked the big (and somewhat anti-climactic) reveal at the conclusion. It showed a surprising amount of heart for a book that seemed like it was destined to turn into one gigantic love letter to present and future Google executives. But maybe I read it all wrong. Maybe there's a secret code in there, hiding the real meaning of the whole thing...d to turn into one gigantic love letter to present and future Google executives. But maybe I read it all wrong. Maybe there's a secret code in there, hiding the real meaning of the whole thing...

Just as I feared, Sesto Bruscantini as Pasquale fails to provide weight or enough buffo to pull this off. He sounds so much lighter than Leo Nucci (Dr. Malatesta) that the only way to tell them apart is Pasquale has the lower notes. As for Nucci, his upper range is wonderful but his fioratura is very sluggish. Freni, one of my all-time favorite sopranos is terribly mis-cast. She can turn a phrase and be coy and demure, but lacks the agility and lightness in the upper register to make this soubrette role hers. At times the ensembles sound like early Verdi with her full lyric sound. He later moved into heavier repertoire but in 1984. His vocal timbre is dead on for the role of Ernesto, but in the higher range he has marked trouble with the tessitura's demands. In the famously difficult Act 2 scene of 'Povero Ernesto - Cerchero lontana terra', he struggled helplessly and landed on an octave low C sharp at the end of the aria.  He is, in short, not as good as Matthew Polenzani (with the low C sharp), nor as good as JDF (who has the high C sharp), and is way behind Alfredo Kraus and Francisco Araiza in this role (both with the absolutely sound high tessitura and drop dead beautiful C sharp to boot).

It takes place during the summer of1965, on a sparsely populated island somewhere in New England. Twelve-year-old Sam Shakusky (Jared Gilman) has resigned his commission and gone AWOL with a miniature canoe and some supplies from a Khaki Scout camp under the command of Scout Master Ward (Edward Norton). The local authority, police Captain Sharp (Bruce Willis), goes looking for Sam only to discover that Suzy Bishop (Kara Hayward) is also missing from her parents' home. The young couple have apparently run off together, just as a hurricane works its way up the coast.<br /><br />Sam and Suzy have a hard time getting along with people, but they see themselves in each other and hit it off right away. In spite of their frustrations, they're full of youthful optimism and a yearning for adventure. And they go out and have that adventure, leaving the adults to worry and search frantically for them. These two young actors are very appealing, and their antics, however eyebrow-raising are sympathetic and funny. The adults are also sympathetic, if a bit disengaged from life until this incident galvanizes them. -With the exception of a woman representing social services (Tilda Swinton), who wants to have Sam committed. She seems to represent the menace of the mainland, where people do things differently than on the friendly, laid back island.<br /><br />I love the period touches -Suzy's minidresses and blue eye shadow, record player, and less neurotic, simpler, dispositions in general. But \\"Moonrise Kingdom\\" is not a period film. Anderson uses 1960s motifs when it suits him and anachronisms just as easily. Sam and Suzy are more romantically sophisticated than sheltered middle class kids were before the internet. Suzy's parents are both lawyers, which leaves me to wonder who takes care of her three little brothers if her mother works long hours. There were not many female lawyers in the 1960s, much less with young children. The couple is also old to have children that age by the standards of their generation. It's Wes Anderson's whimsical universe, not 1960s America.ers if her mother works long hours. There were not many female lawyers in the 1960s, much less with young children. 0520224787|5.0|Robert's translation comes at Three Kingdoms from an academic vantage. His afterword is exception as are his notes very thorough. His prose is exceptionally readable and delightfully entertaining<br /><br />That said, this edition itself is somewhat frustration to use. All the notes appear at the end of volume 2, meaning you'll need to carry around both books and constantly flip between pages to take advantage of them. If you are interested in the text as an academic work, this is very frustrating; of course if you just want to read, this keeps all the research out of your face. I would have liked to have seen Robert's hard work more prominent in the work--footnotes instead of end notes and more maps and figures.<br /><br />With that said, this is without question the best translation of the Sangouzhi tongsu yanyi. The question is which version do you want to read. This is probably the best and more affordable option. There is also a cheaper 4-volume paperback and an expensive Chinese-English parallel text version. Don't read the abridged version unless you have a professor who is afraid to assign a 1,000 page novel to undergrads :)

B0002WZTOI|4.0|Tony Scott's \\"Top Gun\\" was obviously built on the template of \\"[[ASIN:B00003CXBT An Officer and a Gentleman]]\\" and was a mega-hit in May/June of 1986.<br /><br />THE PLOT: Two hotshot Navy pilots, Maverick (Tom Cruise) and Goose (Anthony Edwards), are sent to a prestigious flight school in San Diego where they must endure the rivalry of other pilots, like Iceman (Val Kilmer). Maverick seeks a relationship with one of the school's civilian instructors (Kelly McGillis) and also faces a crisis when his cocky confidence is shaken.<br /><br />\\"Top Gun\\" is basically a modern \\"[[ASIN:B00008AOTN The Blue Max]]\\" in that it mixes the drama on the ground with the excitement in the air. It's a good mix that keeps it from being one-dimensional.<br /><br />Some criticize the film as being superficial fluff but, while \\"Top Gun\\" is definitely a blockbuster, it actually has some credible depth. For example, the rivalry of the pilots, the mystery of Maverick's father, the grievous death of one of the main characters, and Maverick's crisis of confidence. A good example of the film's depth can be seen in the scene where Iceman confronts Maverick in the locker room after a tragedy. Iceman is sincere but walks on eggshells because he respects Maverick's unpredictable and dangerous nature. The scene rings true-to-life.<br /><br />Tom Skerritt is notable as one of the older instructors of the school, Viper. There's a good scene in the 2nd half where Maverick visits Viper's house on a Sunday, which features a great (funny) line from Skerritt (\\"I'm not going to blow sunshine...\\").<br /><br />Unfortunately, the film has been accused of being somehow \\"homo-erotic.\\" Nonsense. In case these clueless critics didn't notice, Maverick is chasing McGillis' character throughout the film and even \\"breaks into\\" a Ladies Room to see her. Meanwhile Goose is happily married with children. As for the locker room scenes and the all-male volley ball game, the story takes place at a flight school where all the students are MALE. The volley ball sequence is just a fun scene, nothing more, and was likely thrown in for the ladies. Besides, notice that Maverick leaves the game prematurely to go see HIS BABE. I can't help but wonder if these criticizers are projecting their OWN ISSUES on to the film. Enough said.<br /><br />On the downside, there are some cringe-inducing scenes, like the aforementioned one in the Ladies Room with its awkward dialogue. A minor flaw is that the film starts to lose its drive by the final act, maybe because it drags on and should've been edited. The film runs 110 minutes, by the way.<br /><br />\\"Top Gun\\" has a decent mid-80's soundtrack highlighted by Kenny Loggins' \\"Danger Zone.\\" Speaking of the soundtrack, Judas Priest's excellent track \\"Reckless\\" off of [[ASIN:B004IY6AH6 Turbo]] was picked by the producers for the soundtrack, but the Priest boys foolishly turned down the offer because (1.) they didn't know who Tom Cruise was since he wasn't a major star until after this movie, (2.) they therefore didn't think the movie would be a hit, and (3.) if they sold the song to the movie it would've been omitted from TURBO. Big mistake because the film was a massive blockbuster and it would've rocketed Priest into superstardom. In any case, listen to \\"Reckless\\" on youtube sometime and you'll see that it would've fit the movie perfectly. It also would've been the heaviest song on the soundtrack by far, even though it's light by Priest's standards.<br /><br />BOTTOM LINE: \\"Top Gun\\" screams mid-80's blockbuster and deservedly so. It's a kinetic film with a nice mix of drama, fun, crisis and aircraft excitement.<br /><br />GRADE: Bstudents are MALE. B00062PN6I|5.0|First of all I'm not going to go on and on about how good these are for the money. Many other reviewers have already made that point very clear. The point I want to make is regarding the issues most of the one star reviews have with this product. Some people claimed they were junk because one side of the phones either didn't work right away or stopped after a certain amount of time. You have to realize that with virtually any type of electronics product, unless it's very high-end, a small percent of that item is going to have defects of one type or another. You can't realistically expect every single copy of a product to be completely perfect, especially when you're talking about one that is made inexpensively by the thousands. If the manufacturer had to thoroughly test every single aspect of each copy you would not be paying that low-end price. It is also important to understand that the number of one star reviews is not comparable to five star reviews percentagewise. The reason for this is due to the fact that if someone is upset and angry about a product they are much more likely to take the time to vent their frustrations by writing a review complaining about the problem they had. On the other hand when a person is satisfied with their purchase their complacency makes the likelyhood of returning to the website and writing a review substantially less. Just imagine how many five star reviews there would be if every satisfied owner wrote a review. So in short more people are likely to write a one star review than a five star. One reviewer said he bought three headphones and one did not work. He therefore surmised that one out of every three headphones was defective. When you consider my first point I explained along with a little intelligent reasoning you can see how this type of logic is totally ridiculous. Another reviewer complained that the headphones were made of cheap plastic. Get real, what did he expect for ten bucks, titanium? Then there was \\"it's a cheap thin cord that will break easily\\". I've owned my headphones for eight months and snagged and yanked on the cord numerous times. The cord has never come close to breaking and is actually a decently thick diameter. For people that claimed the 1/4 inch jack did not fit their port, you simply unscrew the the 1/4 inch tip off the cable end revealing the smaller 1/8 size underneath. To quickly address some of the other complaints: Of course they fit snugly around your ear, how else would they effectively cancel outside noise. I used mine for hours every day for eight months and the stitching is nowhere near coming apart. The soft earpads make the fit very comfortable, and they're very easy to adjust. The final verdict is simple. If you can possibly find a better pair of headphones for ten bucks then buy them. I say Good Luck.thin cord that will break easily\\". Although I still loved it I wished that NO DOUBT or any band/artist could release an album equal to it. So began a musical purgatory in my life. Nothing sounded great, like TRAGIC KINGDOM. Then the band released Rock Steady. At the time, I thought it was strange that the band was trying to penetrate the reggae market. Many of the songs on ROCK STEADY were what I needed to spark my interest in music again. I was worried about the direction of the band because of all the reggae influence. I went back and listened to RETURN OF SATURN and saw that the band was just evolving their sound with each record. I then became intranced by certain songs on both records, awing at the talent of that each band member has and refined sound that I think Tragic Kingdom lacked, being such a raw album itself. This elegance made its way onto the band's single/remake of IT'S MY LIFE.<br /><br />Then began the hiatus of No Doubt, which included Gwen's solo career, which was OK, but not what I had come to expect from the collaboration of the band & their affiliates. Band member, Tony Kanal, did help P!NK with FUNHOUSE. I can totally see a NO DOUBT influence sparking the music and lyrics behind this P!nk album. This is maybe why I love the record so much and one I hold to a similar standard to NO DOUBT's previous compilations.<br /><br />So here we are ... the recent past and current present. After my own musical renaissance in college, the force of music came flooding back into my life stronger than ever, becoming a love of  mine again. I began following the band again. I listened to every album many times over. I learned to love each album on its own. I thought that if this was all NO DOUBT would ever do together than I would have to follow them separately. I settled for thinking I would have to get my NO DOUBT fix vicariously through those artists they chose to light the flame of greatness beneath.<br /><br />BUT THEN, the band announced that they were working on a new album. I eagerly anticipated its release even through its delayed release (to the agnst of their fans) and my delayed order from Amazon. The best stunt they could have done is release a song telling fans to SETTLE DOWN and that is exactly what they did! Just one more reason to love NO DOUBT. Not only that, but Settle Down is such a silly song that kinda has a weird fit to the puzzle of PUSH AND SHOVE as is the title track. One thing that I have seen in the progress of NO DOUBT is that they have been increasingly slipping into the background of music (I see parallels to Alanis Morissette). TRAGIC KINGDOM being their big breakout success that went further than they could have ever dreamed. They created an album that set the bar. Everything from their looks through to their entertainment factor pushed the envelope. This continued into RETURN OF SATURN, which despite not being as successful as TRAGIC KINGDOM still set the bar for alternative/pop rock. With ROCK STEADY they hadcrazy fusion between pop, rock, electronica and reggae, but it worked. They were conforming somewhat, but they were still pushing their fanbase into new territory. PUSH AND SHOVE seems like a move into the background. Almost a fading out if you will, which would have made sense like 5 years ago. But Why put out a CD if you don't think you are going to continue making music together?<br /><br />Despite this factor and what many others say, I love PUSH AND SHOVE and I think it was worth the wait. My only complaint is that I think that Gwen could have sung some of the songs with a little more passion or displayed some kind of variation throughout each work. The record feels like a glimpse into the soul of the band and where they were up to where they are presently, which deserves a little more conviction on Gwen's part. Just like a NO DOUBT album though, each song is unique and fresh. So its not the band's best work, but its still a fantastic collaboration between its talented members.crazy fusion between pop, rock, electronica and reggae, but it worked. This is NOT the album that was bangin' in the clubs, in our cars, or at our house parties.  Take it from someone who was there, this so-called \\"remaster\\" is not just an enhancement of sound quality as the name might imply, it's a totally different album.<br /><br />Don't get it twisted, the original version, the one with the white cover, wasn't some rough mix that was stolen from Easy Mo Bee's basement and released on the streets as a bootleg or whatever...it was the official studio release.  The one you bought at Sam Goody, Coconuts, or, until 2006, right here on amazon.  And now it's gone forever in favor of this inferior mess.<br /><br />And why?  Money, mostly.  And a touch of political correctness.<br /><br />1.) Bad Boy's legal department apparently f'd up and some of the samples used on the original weren't cleared properly, so rather than tap into their billions and just pay whatever licensing fees were necessary for the re-release, Diddy and company decided to just CHANGE THE ORIGINALS!!!  So now, tracks like \\"Machine Gun Funk\\" and \\"Ready to Die\\" sound totally different.  They are not at all what we heard when we first bumped this album back in '94.<br /><br />2.) Some of Biggie's original lyrics were apparently too raw for the sensibilities of the new millenium so they were edited out or backmastered.  Most notably on \\"Juicy\\" where he spits \\"time to get paid/blow up like the World Trade\\" referencing the 1993 attack on the towers.  On the remaster, the words \\"World Trade\\" are edited out, presumably because someone might think he was making a reference to 9/11 seven years before it actually happened.  While I understand that 9/11 was a catastrophic and horrible event, and would certainly agree that a rapper using it as a euphemism for accruing wealth would be unbelievably crass, I also don't think that record companies should go back and selectively edit albums that came out seven years before the tragedy even happened because someone might think that Biggie was Nostradamus and predicted the whole thing in his crystal ball, thus compromising his original vision and lyricism.<br /><br />Now that this \\"remaster\\" has come out, the only way to get the original is to run it down in some used record store.  Think about what this means.  Kids who grew up hearing that Biggie was the best and wanting to hear the album that their elders say prove it will rush to purchase or download this \\"remaster\\", because it's the only thing available, not realizing that they are NOT hearing what those of us who copped the original heard back in '94.  They're not hearing Biggie as we heard him.  They're not hearing his magnum opus.  They're hearing a compromised, mutilated version of that album. Again, think about what this says about Bad Boy's respect for their greatest artist, the man whose talent they pretty much rode to wealth and glory. Would anyone dare to dream of doing this to the Beatles' \\"Sgt. Pepper's\\", Bob Marley's \\"Catch a Fire\\" or Marvin Gaye's \\"What's Going On\\"?  No?  Then what does this say about Bad Boy's respect for Biggie and hip hop as an artform in general?<br /><br />Because it's Biggie, I can't bring myself to give even this mangled version of his vision one star, but because this musical mutilation is the auditory equivalent of putting boxer shorts on Donatello's David or a bra on the Venus de Milo, I also can't bring myself to give it more than two.<br /><br />To the young hip hop headz out there, consider yourselves warned. B000000OXH|5.0|\\"Alpha\\" came out in 1983 as the followup to the band's eponymous debut, but was not well-received either critically or commercially (it went double-platinum, but compared to the debut album it followed, it was a significant disappointment).  The flaws in this album, both cultural and aesthetic, are well-documented, and I won't go too deeply into them here.  The bottom line is this:  suddenly Asia was seen as a band that wasn't \\"cool.\\"  (Not only did they steal Yes's instrumental style - they also inherited their reputation.)<br /><br />However, I loved this album when it came out, and I still do today.  I would love a remastered version to crisp up the sound - Steve Howe and Carl Palmer did wonderful work, when you can hear it, but the mixing technique used seems to drown them out at times. This is a shame, because Steve Howe's guitar work is spectacular, and Palmer's drum work would add a lot simply by being double-tracked.<br /><br />The downfall of Asia's first incarnation was always its lyrics - this was evident from their first single release (name another top-10 single released between 1981 and 1987 that uses the word \\"disco\\" ANYWHERE.  OK - Hungry Like the Wolf? Fine. Name another) - and Alpha's one shortcoming is lyrical.  The Wetton-Downes duo has since matured, and the new reincarnation features greatly improved lyric work, but on this album, there is an oversimplification of some concepts (and some stilted constructs) that diminishes some of the musical work with word choices that at times are average at best.<br /><br />Musically, the melodies and arrangements range from the merely very good (\\"The Last To Know,\\" \\"True Colors,\\" \\"Don't Cry\\") to absolutely wonderful (\\"Open Your Eyes,\\" \\"Midnight Sun\\").  If I were banished to a desert island and were allowed only one recorded song to hear for the rest of my life, I would choose \\"Open Your Eyes,\\" and the only reason I would even hesitate would be its bookend from the Omega album (\\"There Was A Time\\").<br /><br/>If you were alive and socially aware in 1983 when this album was released, I suggest a new listen, without prejudice.  I don't claim perfection here - this is a very good album that should have been great, but wasn't (in no small part by virtue of mob opinion) - a shortcoming for which this band was unduly, and in my eyes, unjustly punished.  Asia deserved better, and even now as they are back together and releasing new (and excellent) work, I hope they will bring together something that rises beyond the sum of their very, very talented parts.<br /><br />Until then, I have \\"Alpha\\" as the soundtrack of my teenage years, and \\"Open Your Eyes\\" as the song I played long ago for a girl with a wounded heart, whom I had watched and been near for two years without hope, on the day she so unexpectedly realized that I was who she wanted.  Looking back, it wasn't the touchstone moment of my life (see above reference), but music strikes the poignancy in us as well as the passion.  This album, for me, connects with both.

He does this with a good dose of humor.) The book includes a variety of patterns and plans.<br /><br />This is my first book on paddlemaking, and, despite my lack of woodworking experience, I think it will be enough to keep me educated and occupied for quite a while. As you might expect, if you are familiar with Thor, Iron Man, and Captain America, these are some bold and strong-willed personalities coming together, and in that kind of situation, you have a lot of potential for conflict.  Mark Ruffalo plays a great understated Bruce Banner, and the animation of the Hulk character really reflects Ruffalo visually, which lends to the character's credibility.  His personality balances the team well, and the military backgrounds brought by Hawkeye and Black Widow offer more to the story than might be expected, when outshone by the rest of the team.<br /><br />Whedon excellently crafts these conflicts, playing the characters off one another well.  Bringing them together NATURALLY despite their conflicts is something that could have posed a great challenge, but Whedon finds a way to unify them without ever appearing to force its change.  Bringing together references from the entire Marvel Universe proves fairly successful, and even the small characters contribute to the story progression in their own ways.<br /><br />Ultimately there's little doubt that between the epic, heavy conflict, and the light-hearted comedic quips, Whedon has a great success on his hands.  For anyone interested in superhero action or the individual characters that have been crafted over the past several years, The Avengers is a must see.ry progression in their own ways.<br /><br />Ultimately there's little doubt that between the epic, heavy conflict, and the light-hearted comedic quips, Whedon has a great success on his hands.  For anyone interested in superhero action or the individual characters that have been crafted over the past several years, The Avengers is a must see.

B00A3AUGEW|2.0|Phillip Phillips releases 2012's [[ASIN:B009NPA3MS World From the Side of the Moon]] off of notoriety based on winning the most recent American Idol season and off the popularity of his crowing single used during the Olympics \\"Home.\\" Indeed those triumphs certainly aided in promoting the southern boy's debut, which bowed at no. 4 with 169,000 copies - not too shabby. While the support is there, World From The Side of The Moon is an album that will be more embraced by 'fans' from the show as opposed to say new fans.  World From The Side of the Moon certainly isn't the most dreadful album of 2012, but neither is it a 'second coming' as suggested by some freely endorsing it with 5 star reviews.  The main issue with this effort is the identity crisis that Phillips suffers - who is the real Phillip Phillips? Too much of the album seems to imitate the cues of Dave Matthews, Mumford & Sons, and previous/current artists in those respective styles. Add some 'raw' songwriting by Phillips that could use some tweaks to better lay on the effort as a whole, and The World From the Side of the Moon has some issues.<br /><br />The first three cuts of the album are the strongest and set up World From the Side of the Moon with great promise.  \\"Man on the Moon\\" opens with rhythmic acoustic guitar work and establishes a sound harmonic progression. A Phillips original, \\"Man on the Moon\\" is the best of Phillips's songwriting.  Phillips channels his 'idol' Matthews, but manages to gie an overall capable performance. The chorus is wordy, but you can't deny the poetry of the lyrics: \\"Hold on it won't take long/you can find yourself if you decide to finally start/but don't look to me when you fall/because the steps get bigger so go ahead and walk them off/you know how I feel/so don't let your life start to waste away...\\"<br /><br />\\"Home\\" is an easy home run for Phillips, a record that continues to grow on you with successive listens.  Vocally, Phillips sounds his most polished, a comment not often associated with the anti-melodic singer throughout American Idol.  Drawing from Mumford & Sons, \\"Home\\" does something that later tracks fail to do - sound distinctly Phillip Phillips and not a copycat of some other artist.<br /><br />The final gem of the trio is \\"Gone, Gone, Gone,\\" a song with strong songwriting structure and memorable chorus: \\"For you for you/baby I'm not movin' on/I'll love you long after you're gone...\\" If there is a quibble, the overall sound seems a bit too light - and that's nitpicking ultimately.<br /><br />The album begins to 'lose' its strength following \\"Man On the Moon,\\" \\"Home,\\" and \\"Gone, Gone, Gone.\\" \\"Hold On\\" marks the beginning of Phillips's identity crisis as he overreaches in channeling Matthews, particularly in his lower register.  Another original, the songwriting itself overreaches for serious thematic material causing it to become bland, background music.<br /><br />\\"Tell Me A Story\\" fails to atone for \\"Hold On,\\" feeling even more like a generic Dave Matthews cut.  A bit over dramatic, Phillips again tries 'too hard' here, evidenced particularly on the chorus: \\"Alone is the street where you found me/scared of what's behind you/ scared of what's in front...\\" Both \\"Hold On\\" and \\"Tell Me A Story\\" don't capture the magic of the trio that captivates the beginning of the album, which is unfortunate.<br /><br />\\"Get Up Get Down\\" is an improvement, particularly given a quicker pace.  Hurting the 'B' cut it feels like Dave Matthews, epitomized.  Very much like cuts I reviewed from Dave Matthew Band's [[ASIN:B008FERRFO Away From The World (Deluxe Version)]], the horns and riffs characterize the cut.  Sure, this is a Phillip Phillips co-written cut on a Phillip Phillips album and not Dave Matthews, but in an industry like music where a balance between individual and conformity, the record may not sound 'distinctly' like Phillip Phillips as opposed to his influences.<br /><br />\\"Where We Came From,\\" the second single, executes more similar to tracks 1-3.  There is clear songwriting form and Phillips sounds more like only Phillip Phillips.  Part of the reason for this is that he ascends into his more melodic upper register, which allows for him to show of a more distinct voice and more personality, particularly on the memorable pre-chorus/chorus: \\"Climb the mountain, swim for the shore/bring it back to how it was before//take it out, blow it up/ignite the memory in between us...\\" \\"Where We Came From\\" is within the top four of the effort.<br /><br />\\"Drive Me\\" features some solid pieces (more of a rock sound, instrumental ideas, and chorus), but also has some flaws. Phillips's voice is inconsistent, particularly throughout the verses.  While the saxophone solo is nice, it is predictable because it takes listeners directly back to a firmly established Dave Matthews Band.<br /><br />Follow-up cut \\"Wanted Is Love\\" initiates as what sounds as if it will be a ballad, but the gargantuan refrain plays spoils to that notion. Again, Phillips writes/sings loftily here: \\"Wanted is love, not going insane/you know you've got to hold onto what you love before it's gone away...\\" It's ok, but as with so much of World From the Side of the Moon, its not necessarily memorable. \\"Can't Go Wrong\\" again lacks artistic distinction, borrowing Mumford & Son's signature rhythmic banjo on the chorus.  More against this cut is over repetition and again Phillips 'trying too hard' to evoke emotion.<br /><br />Penultimate cut \\"A Fool's Dance\\" is characterized by rhythm by the guitars, a feature that is overdone throughout this album.  Again, there are some sound pieces in place (background vocals, foreboding strings), but along with the 'good' comes 'bad.' While only marginally lengthy at 4:33, the cut feels too drawn out and ultimately lacking focus.  Closing cut \\"So Easy\\" sports Phillips's surprising falsetto as a highlight, but suffers similarly from over repetition and feeling 'too serious' and 'lofty.'<br /><br />All-in-all, [[ASIN:B009NPA3MS World From the Side of the Moon]] is as clunky as its title. As suggested throughout this critique, there are many promising 'pieces' that shine through this debut. Unfortunately aside from ace-in-the-hole \\"Home\\" and a few other standouts, the rest of the album is flawed.  Phillips sings ok, certainly with more sense of melody than while on American Idol, but the charisma he could showcase on live TV doesn't translate to the oft humdrum material of The World From the Side of the Moon.imilar to tracks 1-3.  There is clear songwriting form and Phillips sounds more like only Phillip Phillips. Phillips sings ok, certainly with more sense of melody than while on American Idol, but the charisma he could showcase on live TV doesn't translate to the oft humdrum material of The World From the Side of the Moon.

B005FVFWOI|4.0|To many listeners, \\"Aqualung\\" may be the best, or even the \\"only\\" Jethro Tull recording.  While I may not feel quite so strongly about it, I like this album, and have respect for it creatively and musically.  I was disappointed in previous CD versions of it, and having read a range of reviews for this remastered 2011 release, both positive and negative, I decided I should hear it for myself.<br /><br />Something significant was discovered listening to the first few seconds of the album:  the famous six-note guitar line that opens the title track is heard twice.  This is in fact the correct, original introduction, with the drums entering only after the guitar has repeated the opening figure.  Playing an early vinyl LP of \\"Aqualung\\" I owned years ago had been the last time, until this CD, that I had heard it presented this way.  Later LP pressings and subsequent releases in several configurations dropped the first guitar line.  This confounded me for years just as, I can well imagine, hearing this restoration may baffle anyone who has never before heard the introduction in its original form.<br /><br />Musically, \\"Aqualung\\" is quite impressive, and great credit is due to all members of Jethro Tull, who do a skillful turn realizing Ian Anderson's eclectic, complex music.  Guitarist Martin Barre, who joined the band on \\"Stand Up\\", their second album, struggled a bit on that one, but by the next album (\\"Benefit\\") the refinement of his playing had taken a giant stride.  Next came \\"Aqualung\\", and his performance here, rightly, won him quite a bit of acclaim.  I might also give a special nod to keyboardist John Evan, who first worked with Tull on \\"Benefit\\".  A classically-trained performer, his playing seems specially suited to some of the more baroque moments in this music.<br /><br />Some reviewers give this CD a low rating on the basis of its sound.  I do not take issue with them, as we all hear things in an individual way.  However, I think the sound is about as good ascan be expected, given several factors.  For one thing, CDs just simply have limitations.  Listeners comparing any CD with a vintage vinyl LP of the same music are likely to be disappointed with the former.  In addition, I have heard (not to be quoted here) that the master tape of \\"Aqualung\\" has been lost.  If this is true, there is no telling what was used as a source recording for this current disc.  The 1996, 25th Anniversary release was mastered using special noise reduction technology, raising questions about the source tape then as well.  On this new one, I can detect that attention was given to capturing the dynamic range and, as much as may be possible, the ambient qualities of the original recording.  So, if this one is not perfect, it sounds better to me than earlier CD versions (I should mention that I have not heard the DCC gold disc), and is a worthy effort.<br /><br />The second disc in the set contains some tracks which have been released previously, and a few that have not, all mastered with the same care as the featured album.  It is very nice to have 'Wond'ring Again' included, this time appearing as a kind of extended coda built onto 'Wond'ring Aloud', its companion track from \\"Aqualung\\".  This conjoined version has evidently not been released before, making it seem a worthwhile addition and not just a gimmick.<br /><br />My rating of four stars can be read as four-and-a-half.  I think it is about as good as anything we will see on compact disc.  If this music on CD sounded more like the vinyl record did (which may not be possible), and if a few details such as the inclusion of printed lyrics had been seen to, this would easily rate five stars.

B00007LTIC|5.0|\\"Going for the One\\" was a brilliant return to form for Yes, and a necessary one, too -- without this 1977 album and the new pathway it provided for the band to move forward, I think it's entirely possible Yes would have broken up.<br /><br />Yes had had some amazing successes at the time this album was recorded. \\"The Yes Album,\\" \\"Fragile\\" and \\"Close to the Edge\\" were, each and every one, monumental art rock classics. From the tough-minded riffing of \\"Yours Is No Disgrace\\" on \\"The Yes Album\\" to the FM hit \\"Roundabout\\" on \\"Fragile\\" to the lyrical \\"And You and I\\" from \\"Close to the Edge,\\" the songs were sure, powerful and graceful.<br /><br />And then, at the height of its powers, Yes seemed to lose its way. \\"Tales From Topographic Oceans,\\" a 2-LP issue back in those vinyl days, drove keyboardist Rick Wakeman from the band; he quit after its release, flummoxed by the approach: Four sidelong suites of music, inspired by the Indian shastric scriptures, that just didn't seem to hold together the way the title track for \\"Close to the Edge\\" had. \\"Relayer,\\" the followup from 1974, featured Patrick Moraz filling in for the departed Wakeman, and consisted of a single LP featuring two tracks on side two (\\"Sound Chaser,\\" \\"To Be Over\\") and side one's sidelong \\"The Gates of Delirium.\\" The album was even more of a mess than \\"Topographic\\" was, with Yes descending so far into dissonance on some tracks (\\"Sound Chaser\\" especially) that even some of the group's hardcore fans found it difficult to follow.<br /><br />Note: To be fair, I should acknowledge that \\"Topographic\\" and \\"Relayer\\" have gained some stature over the years. I myself listen to them infrequently, and do enjoy sections of both albums, especially \\"Topographic's\\" concluding piece, \\"Ritual (Nous Sommes Du Soleil).\\"<br /><br />Yes, itself, seemed to sense this loss of direction; \\"Relayer\\" was released in 1974 and it would be three years before \\"Going For the One\\" saw daylight in 1977. Part of that time was taken up, of course, by each of the five band members releasing solo albums in 1975.<br /><br />When \\"Going for the One\\" did arrive in stores, fans and even critics of Yes were pleased. The album opened with the title track, which packed a lot of gritty rock 'n' roll into just five and a half minutes, thanks in no small measure to Steve Howe's snarling guitars. \\"Turn of the Century\\" was a beautiful piece of lyric writing from vocalist Jon Anderson, supported by musical input from Howe and drummer Alan White. Side one concluded with \\"Parallels,\\" an amazing track by bassist Chris Squire that featured Wakeman's excellent performance on the pipe organ at St. Martins Church in Vevey, Switzerland.<br /><br />None of the three songs on side one exceeded eight minutes in length. Side two began with one that clocked in at just under four, Anderson's beautiful (and radio friendly!) \\"Wonderous Stories.\\"<br /><br />Yes did revert to the long-song format for the album's final song. But while much of \\"Relayer\\" especially seemed like indulgent noodling, \\"Awaken\\" clearly was a piece that had been thought out thoroughly by its composers, Anderson and Howe. Its 15:31 running time began with a nimble piano figure from Wakeman, followed by a vocal introduction from Anderson that led into the song's main groove. The interlude featured more of Wakeman's playing on the St. Martins pipe organ, this time showing him in a reflective mood as opposed to his aggressive work on \\"Parallels.\\"<br /><br />Over the years, \\"Going For the One\\" has become one of my \\"go-to\\" Yes albums. It's great to put it on and experience, once again, the combination that worked when this band was at its peak: A mix of power, grace and confidence. I highly recommend it.e, by each of the five band members releasing solo albums in 1975.<br /><br />When \\"Going for the One\\" did arrive in stores, fans and even critics of Yes were pleased. Also, these scripts are much better written than the clunky twaddle that passes for dialogue in the Twilight films.  Of course, as all true genre fans know, the boy vampire will try heroically to deny his evil nature in order to win his girl's love.  This struggle never ends, but will always be continued next week, and always include a touching final scene accompanied by a sweet pop song.  I may sound a bit cynical here, but, in fact, these moments usually bring a tear to my eye.<br /><br />Possibly the most surprising and curious thing about this show may be its bizarre chastity.  Having hired all those comely actors, the producers never let us see them naked, even when having sex.  This is in contrast to True Blood, which tends to take nudity and sex to campy excess.  So what is it about Vampire Diaries that makes it work?  Here's one suggestion:  The photography and direction are veryfine and every shot is beautifully illuminated against dark shadows like a Vermeer painting.  (True Blood, by contrast, tends to look quite gaudy).  This subtlety of design and lighting suits these ancient creatures.<br /><br />Finally, there is actor Ian Sommerhalder, who plays the bad brother Damon (or is he the good brother?). Perhaps he is the series' secret weapon.<br /><br /> In sum, then, the classic simplicity of Vampire Diaries easily beats the overwrought extravagance of True Blood and the lame dialogue of the Twilight series, and earns my vote as the best of the genre.  I will be back for the next season.

With their brightly colored clothing and  outgoing ways, Vianne and Anouk  stand out like macaws in a flock of crows. Both Vianne and Reynaud have deep secrets and Vianne earns Reynaud's enmity almost at once by opening a chocolate shop- which would be bad enough in his view, but to add insult to injury, she does it at the beginning of Lent, when Reynaud wants all to deny themselves any kind of pleasure. At first he feels she will fail quickly, but she has a touch not just with candy making but with people- she has the ability to know what people want or need. When she announces plans for a chocolate festival to be held on Easter Sunday, it's war.<br /><br /> This is a work of magical realism, but one where the magic is denied. We're never entirely sure it's real... but despite the denial, there are some pretty strong signs it is. It's also a book about jealousy, prejudice, the value of being true to one's self, aging with &eacute;lan, love, loss, abuse, bullying and a lot of other things that make up life no matter where. Told in the alternating, first person POVs of Vianne and Reynaud, the book opens their pasts enough to us so we know why they act as they do, but leaves enough unsaid to keep us wanting more. The descriptive prose is glittering: the chocolates, the wrappings, the foods, the wine and champagne all appear in three dimensions and five senses. Don't read this book if you are dieting; it provokes cravings that, in my case at least, will not be denied. A beautiful book.

0671027344|2.0|I was kind of expecting to like this book, because everyone else I know who's read it has described it with words like \\"amazing\\" and \\"powerful\\" and told me how important it was to them and how much they related to it.  So I tried.  I really did.  Even when the main character burst into tears 15 times in 10 pages, sobbing anytime someone was nice to him.  I tried to put myself in his 15-year-old shoes, but it still left a bad taste in my mouth.<br /><br />I knew this book and I were not going to like each other about the time I got to that dreadful poem.  If you think that is good poetry, then I am going to gently suggest you make a trip to a library or book store and visit the poetry section.  As a lover of poetry (both classical and contemporary), I have to say that the poem in this book is not even bad in a way I can make fun of.  It's just trite and useless.  I am assuming that the author of the book wrote it, because no serious poet could get that published outside of the context of a young adult novel.  I hope.  Please, god, don't let poetry sink that far into self-indulgent tripe.<br /><br />It just tried SO HARD.  Around every corner was suicide, rape, abortion, drinking, drug use, bullying, violence, sex, depression, child abuse, family problems and low self-esteem.  I'm not disputing that those are all serious, important issues and worthy material for a novel.  I AM disputing that I have to like a book just because the author brought that stuff up.  It felt...cheap.  Like a big shortcut that he thought should automatically lead to substance.  In real life?  Yeah, that's substance.  On paper?  Nope. Not unless you deal with it in any sort of realistic or meaningful way (or at least humanize it, for god's sake).<br /><br />I was talking to my brother about it, and I exclaimed, \\"But he's not even interesting!  He's just an empty shell of a human being, and not in a fun way!\\"<br /><br />And here's the thing: I was DEFINITELY sort of a weird kid, an outsider among the various high school cliques, a shy girl who cried too much about silly things.  And I definitely struggled with depression, low self-esteem, not feeling like I was really a part of things.  So I kept feeling like I ought to be more sympathetic, but I couldn't be.  I just kept thinking, \\"how can anyone be this inexcusably BORING?\\"<br /><br />But maybe that's not what gets me.  If someone in real life were that boring, it would be different.  It's more affronting to me that I am expected to want to READ about this kid's bland-ass, clichd life observations.  Even when he's dropping acid at parties, getting into fistfights and screwing around with a girl he doesn't even like, he STILL manages to make it dull--mostly by crying through all of it.  And not even describing HOW he cried; he usually just says, \\"then I started crying.\\"<br /><br />In all fairness, there were parts of this book that I did like.  Namely, any parts that were about Charlie's friends, rather than Charlie himself.  If I'd hated every page, I wouldn't have finished reading it (or maybe I would have--I'm contrary like that).  But that made me feel even worse, after I'd finished it.  I WANTED to like it.  I could ALMOST like it.  But not quite.  It was like being in a relationship with someone who's wretchedly, terribly wrong for you, but every so often they'll surprise you with flowers or dinner or say something nice, and it makes you relent a little bit until you end up staying with them way longer than you ever would or should have if they'd never bothered at all.<br /><br />I will say that it made me feel much better about my own 15-year-old self.  Sure, I was a lot of gloom and doom, and sometimes when I read old journal entries from that time, I kind of want to drown past-me in a toilet.  But at least I had a personality.  I was a human being.  Charlie is...worse than a robot.  He's bad fiction trying to be deep.
B00003CXA6|5.0|Okay, so it's not entirely historically accurate.  I majored in History and I got over that, so everyone else should too.  Tom Berenger and Jeff Daniels give two of the most incredible performances I have seen on film.  The \\"extras\\" are actually civil war reenactors who went to Gettysburg and camped on the battlefield (with permission) to make this film.  When Martin Sheen needed to check a pocket watch on film, the producers just got one from the extras, knowing that it would be period-accurate!<br /><br />It's long.  Running time is about 3 hours 30 minutes, but it is worth it!  The film covers the three days of battle and the two days on either side, so it covers the set up and the aftermath.  Finally, this is the last film performance by Richard Jordan (he portrays Gen. Armistead, the man who physically led \\"Pickett's Charge\\"), and his performance is simply amazing.<br /><br />The film's authentic feel and true emotional performances rise above any of the minor historical problems.  Leave those issues in another room and watch this film sometime around July 1st through 3rd, and bring a box of tissues with you. 0307341550|5.0|SHARP OBJECTS had never truly been on my radar. I owned a copy (one of the first books I ever bought on my Kindle) but I conveniently managed to forget about it for several months. By several, I mean about 20. It was just after that time where my love of suspense/horror faded for the umpteenth time to be replaced with another obsession. It took awhile to finally come back to it, drawn by an unknown force that propelled me to give it another... well, a first look.<br /><br />Let me just say, this book took me by surprise. It punched me in the gut, shook me, and left me to die on a sidewalk while it giggled at my broken mind.<br /><br />I am generally not a big fan of mysteries, suspense dramas, etc. I rarely read them outside of something that comes highly rated to me. Or at least not since my little departure from the genre awhile back. Falling into the dark, disturbing town of Wind Gap was quite a departure from the ordinary for me. SHARP OBJECTS is a bleak book filled with horrible mother/daughter relationships, obsession, drugs, self-harm, mutilation, and of course murder. It is a mind boggling book that freaked me out from beginning to end. And that's a good thing.<br /><br />Camille Preaker might be one of the strangest heroines (or anti-heroine) you'll ever meet in fiction. Her obsession is with cutting, but being a journalist has put her in a rather precarious spot - her assignment is to go back to her hometown when two girls are brutally murdered and right back into the arms of her very unloving mother, into a home that damaged her permanently for life. With this trip home brings back every memory, every event that turned her into the extremely flawed woman she is today.<br /><br />The massive cast of characters is amazingly complex and well-drawn. Camille herself is a case study in insanity, but you add in her mother (crazy), sister (crazy), friends (crazy), and boss (surprisingly not so crazy), and you have this ingenious look at a town so consumed with the darkness of humanity that even their actions in speaking with one another give you chills. When you get to the actual murders, though, you find yourself looking at some of the most disturbing literature you have read all year.<br /><br />I won't get into explicit detail with this one. Let's just say that SHARP OBJECTS is a novel that must be read to be believed. I finished it in two days (punctuated by work - at which I raved about this one) and immediately knew that Gillian Flynn was a new favorite author. I went out and bought DARK PLACES and GONE GIRL after finishing this.<br /><br />If you are easily freaked out, and if being freaked out freaks you out, then this probably is not the book for you. But otherwise, go and buy this one. It's a few years old but worth it.<br /><br />VERDICT: A disturbing vision of a small town with a dark underbelly, SHARP OBJECTS is one of my favorite reads of 2012. I can't wait to read more of Flynn's work.e darkness of humanity that even their actions in speaking with one another give you chills. 1936608618|5.0|If knowledge is power and speed thrills, then you will want to study every detail in Brian MacKenzie's new book entitled \\"Power Speed Endurance\\".  At 416 pages this book is akin to a college textbook but more valuable in its content and it is bound to become the defacto approach to endurance training.<br /> For anyone familiar with MacKenzie they will know that he and his CrossFit Endurance (CFE) program have begun to question and shift the paradigm in endurance training away from the long slow distance model (LSD) toward a skill based approach to training incorporating the CrossFit strength and conditioning ideology.  This shift in emphasis allows for athletes to develop their technique, reduce their training volume thereby decreasing their likelihood for injury, move more efficiently, recover quicker and perform better.<br /> From beginning to end \\"Power Speed Endurance\\" is full of insights that can only be gleaned from a practitioner as passionate about their profession as MacKenzie.  He introduces the CFE model and philosophy in a common sense manner avoiding a lot of the technical jargon that can prompt a reader to get lost in the details.  Recognizing that running is possibly the most dangerous sport out there, the first chapter is devoted to developing this skill through emphasis on the Pose Running methodology developed originally by Dr. Nicholas Romanov.  This approach is not only sensible but easy enough to learn and follow.  Included within the book are countless pictures, diagrams, exercises and drills to assist the reader in learning.<br /> Doug Katona, the CFE cycling expert, handles the chapter devoted to cycling.  Here the book covers everything from fitting your bike and equipment, to body position, pedal stroke and cornering.  There are even sections covering Time Trials and the relevant mountain bike variations compared to road bikes.<br /> The third and final technique chapter is handled by Chris Michelmore and covers swimming as a skill.  Here you will get great insights into the freestyle stroke and backstroke as these are the two long-axis strokes.  Simply put, these are the two strokes that allow for maximal distance to be covered with minimal energy consumption.  Various drills, breathing techniques and body positions are dissected and explained so that readers can easily implement what they have read into their next training session.<br /> Mackenzie then implements a chapter on strength and conditioning.  This is where the CFE formula starts to put gears into the machine so to speak.  By incorporating a Westside Barbell / CrossFit conditioning conjugate system, MacKenzie is able to demonstrate how endurance athletes can become stronger, faster and more powerful than their peers.  This chapter is where readers will be introduced to a variety of power, strength and gymnastics exercises designed to correct any flaws that exist in their bodies.<br /> Kelly Starrett, who also has a book coming out, devotes a chapter to flexibility.  This chapter alone is a must read whether you are an endurance athlete or couch potato with chronic soft tissue issues.  Take this chapter for a test run and you will surely be as supple as a leopard when you finish.<br /> Nutrition, hydration and electrolyte balance are addressed in the same straight- forward style consistent throughout this book.  Finally, the reader is given a guide on how to make sense of it all when it comes to implementing this training solution on a daily basis.<br /> If you walk into your local book store you would need to purchase multiple books to get the collective insights brought together in this one title.  If you are an endurance athlete with an open mind to less traditional training approaches and you want to set PR's at every turn, then this is the one and only book you will ever need.

B007FEFLTO|2.0|Or, \\"How That Pesky World War II Annoyingly Interrupted Our Sex Lives.\\"<br /><br />\\"Winter of the World\\" by formerly great author Ken Follett is pure made-for-TV soap opera. It isn't literature, not even for  one page, and it's way too long, too boring and too badly written.<br /><br />For example, the desultory, adolescent writing includes this perfect example of how far Follett has descended. From Page 510, \\"After dinner they went to the cinema. The movie was great. Then Woody and Chuck walked the girls back to their apartment. On the way, Woody took Joanne's hand. She smiled and squeezed his hand, and he took that for encouragement.\\" Geez, Mr. Follett, is that the best you can do these days? Or did someone else so creatively write this paragraph? One of your grandchildren? Whatever happened to the Follett we knew in \\"Eye of the Needle\\" and \\"Pillars of the Earth\\"?<br /><br />The fundamental concept for this mostly uninteresting 940-page story is to relate the history of one of the most blockbuster eras the world has ever seen, through the pedestrian lives and loves of a few characters, whose coincidental path-crossing (and long-lost blood relationships) requires a reader to suspend disbelief -- page after page. The pitfalls of this device are 1) abrupt, herky-jerky scene shifts and time warps; 2) unfinished scenarios (the characters simply and magically move on to new adventures without adequate resolution to the previous action; 3) summarily dropped themes and action sequences. Stated simply, the story resembles the old TV sit-com, \\"Days of Our Lives,\\" only it was better.<br /><br />There is much too much reliance on way too often idiotic dialogue to advance the crucial historical/political/social/hegemony story of the time. It's like asking a perfectly sensible but ill-informed shop owner in Missouri to explain the 2012 \\"fiscal cliff\\".<br /><br />Worst of all, the characters, in all their ordinariness, become little more than boring stereotypes. The story is filled with hate, especially toward Russians, even though there are several pro-Soviet enthusiastic characters. While there are many pro-British and pro-American characters, there is not one single believable Nazi. Thus, there is no attempt at balance and virtually no development of the complexity of issues of the time. It boils down to a pro-English speaker's paean. Disappointing, that. Kind of like Faux News.<br /><br />There were some passing good parts. 1) Pearl Harbor, December 1941; 2) Russians taking Berlin in 1945; 3) The rise of women in politics and place in society; 4) 1946 when Churchill's party lost the election in Britain; 5) the atom bomb test in New Mexico in 1945; 6) Explanation of the War in Spain in the 1930s.<br /><br />For the first time in the history of his long writing career, Follett explores the topic of homosexuality in some other way than merely dismissing it as a need-to-be-hidden aberration. Good. Congratulations.<br /><br />He tries desperately to get into the heads and hearts of anti-Nazi Germans throughout the story, though resorts to stick figures and soap-opera uber-drama to do so, resulting in his characters oozing with insincere angst and making childish, panicky decisions.<br /><br />Any characters to admire?  Hmmmm, maybe all those Welsh Williams family members. As I wrote in my review of \\"Fall of Giants\\" (the first of this 3-book trilogy), those Brits remain his best-developed characters.<br /><br />I did read it through to the end. It is not spell-binding nor is it a page-turner, and I never said to myself, \\"Hey, I wonder what's happening to these Follett characters in `Winter of the World'\\"? Nothing about them or the story (other than the already elsewhere documented history of the era) is memorable. For someone like me who loves the history of before, during and after WWII, this book is nothing but a huge let-down and probably will be the last book of Follett's I will ever read. Pity. I really liked some of his earlier works.<br /><br />Thus, sadly, it's a 2.00 on Amazon's rating scale and not anywhere close to being worth the outrageous $19.99 Kindle price. This Giant author has fallen far.br /><br />Thus, sadly, it's a 2.00 on Amazon's rating scale and not anywhere close to being worth the outrageous $19.99 Kindle price. This Giant author has fallen far.

0143039431|4.0|The Grapes of Wrath is a well written, intriguing, darn good book. I was truly impressed by the art and detail that is put into this novel. The book begins with the telling of the truly hospitable conditions that farmers in the south-eastern plains were experiencing. The story follows a family named the Joad's and their desire and pursuit to get to California in search of work, easier times, and a happy life. Tom Joad, who is the main character in the book, is one who I became attached to early on, because of his rash and hasty nature, but kind and merciful attitude. His journey and growth really captured me through-out the whole book.<br /><br />The theme of the book was quite interesting. Humanism, unity, family, and the concept of the Oversoul persist in being the top reasons behind all the events that transpire in the book. The concept of Humanism, family, and the moral reasoning of leaving no man behind are powerful things. Ma Joad, mother of Tom, demonstrates the greatest form of humanism and family, by always wanting to help others in need, and making sure that people were working together to accomplish goals. She is also the one person in the family that is constantly trying to keep the family intact and functioning. Ma even gets physical when she feels her family is going to be broken up. This leads to the next theme, which is unity. Unity is shown in both the camps of people that the Joad's come across, and in a bigger sense of family, the community. The groups of people that the family stumbles across are groups in which everyone had a place, and people worked for the benefit of each other, not themselves. This is something that really takes a mental toll on some of the main characters, who go on to enact their newfound sense of place. Jim Casy, a former preacher, joins the Joad's early on in the book, and is really trying to figure out how to help people who are in need of spiritual help. He comes upon the idea of a shared soul, and no one person being separated from another. This concept of the Oversoul has a profound effect on both Tom and Jim Casy, who make steps towards who they are going to become through-out the book.<br /><br />This is a book that I truly do like, for all the detail and gritty realness of the whole situation that many people were in. However, it can get very dry, very quickly. The first part of the book definitely takes it's time to pick up, which it does, and it becomes very interesting after that point. The character development was excellent and I became enticed with the people surrounding the story.<br /><br />I recommend this book to those who want to read about the harsh conditions and times that people went through, but beware of some long, uninteresting conversations about life.eparated from another. This concept of the Oversoul has a profound effect on both Tom and Jim Casy, who make steps towards who they are going to become through-out the book.<br /><br />This is a book that I truly do like, for all the detail and gritty realness of the whole situation that many people were in. B0041KVW2K|5.0|This is the opinion of a vinyl nerd who has more Beatles records than anyone would need.<br /><br />Either people are imagining defects in their Beatles Vinyl Box, or I hit the lottery with a perfect, unblemished box in every way imaginable.  There is no \\"zipper sound\\" and no \\"string of pearls\\" on any of the LPs.  First and foremost, let me say (with ABSOLUTE confidence) that these sound even better than the CD remasters from '09.  The sound is full, dynamic, and without question worth every penny.  The only critique that I would have is that the vocals at times seem slightly low in the mix.  This is not a problem, at least for me it isn't.  Many people are comparing these to the MFSL vinyl pressings.  I will admit that my Please Please Me MFSL will never be topped, even if it is a bit bright.  Having said that, the Please Please Me in the new box is more than worthy in its own right -- it just has more low end and the vocals are slightly lower in the mix.<br /><br />The book is outrageously gorgeous; it is the book I will use to introduce my children to The Beatles.  No one is disputing the quality of the book, so I won't spend time describing it.<br /><br />With so many complaints about the Abbey Road album from this box, I spent a good amount of time inspecting the vinyl with my eyes and ears -- it's perfect.  In this case, it is BETTER than the MFSL pressing.<br /><br />Finally, I suspect that the remastering process raised the levels of the fade-outs of songs because I am hearing so many things I have never heard before in the thousands of times I have heard these songs.  While I don't think this was \\"intended\\" to be heard in the original mixes -- purists hate any change -- it makes for a better listening experience.<br /><br />So, in closing, I LOVE this box and highly recommend it.

B00192KCQ0|5.0|People think Metallica are lucky to still be around (and not to mention have a large following of fans) after going through some very hostile inner-turmoil (which was well summarized on 2003's \\"Some Kind Of Monster\\" documentary). And some think they are lucky to emerge from a very public lawsuit brought on by drummer Lars Ulrich against Napster's illegal downloading. But what Lars, guitarist Kirk Hammett, vocalist/rhythm guitarist James Hetfield, and newbie bassist Robert Trujillo (who is of Suicidal Tendencies and Ozzy Osbourne fame) are actually lucky to recover from is releasing a string of highly controversial albums. Indeed, 1991's mainstream-breakthrough \\"The Black Album,\\" 1996's and `97's thrash-less, blues-oriented releases (\\"Load\\" and \\"Reload\\"), and 2003's nu-metal-tinged \\"St. Anger\\" all met with mixed reactions from fans everywhere.<br /><br />But Metallica finally rebounded with a new full-length, their ninth, 2008's \\"Death Magnetic.\\" Sounding hungrier than ever before,  the seminal Californian thrash quartet are armed to the teeth with a new arsenal of great riffs and solos, as well as some exceptional drumming and decent bass lines. There are tons of killer hooks present here, too. All of which make \\"D.M\\" a triumphant return to form, and easily one of the best, and most consistent and viscerally satisfying efforts of Metallica's career. Of course, part of what makes this new record so genius is the inclusion of a new producer, Rick Rubin (who has also turned knobs for such heavy metal legends as Slayer and Black Sabbath). His production job is crisp, thunderous, and polished but not overly so. Thus, instead of sanding down the edges on the songs and riffs, Rubin actually sharpens and intensifies them. Plus, Lars' drums sound a lot less overwhelmingly, obnoxiously loud than they were on \\"St. Anger.\\" Sure, Trujillo' bass could stand to be a little bit louder in the mix -- but when the end result is this all-around great, all is easily forgiven.<br /><br />Opener \\"That Wasn't Just Your Life\\" definitely has more-than-enough potential and things going for it to make it a hit single, and a mosh pit-ready new staple in Metallica's live show. It is a loud and abrasive conglomeration of jarring power chords and \\"Ride The Lightning\\"-era blistering thrash riffage. And when a catchy, adherent thrashing groove, some impressive drumming -- including a surprisingly brutal blast beat pattern -- powerful and stirring choruses, and a blazing guitar solo are added to the mix, the end result is an instant classic. \\"The End Of The Line\\" is an explosive and extremely crunchy follow-up that is brimming with cascading, near chainsaw-fast stutter-step riffage. Some catchy, sing-songy choruses, really deft and energetic drumming, and steady, bouncy bass lines are also featured, here, and Kirk tosses in a surprisingly unorthodox, but still very ripping, wah-drenched solo, to boot. But what stands out the most about this song is, again, the riffage -- it is just so razor-sharp and biting that it evokes Eighties-era pure thrash.<br /><br />\\"Broken, Beat & Scarred\\" is immediately engaging, as it weaves sharply hooky, crunching riff slices and forceful drumming through irresistible stop-start hooks. It lets loose another terrific guitar solo, too. Next up, \\"The Day That Never Comes\\" begins sounding like a \\"Black Album\\"-era ballad, and ends up as straight-up, frenetically fast thrash melee. It opens on a pretty and very minor-key note with Kirk weaving subtle, sinewy melodic guitar lines and ambient harmonies, thus adding some depth and variation to the musical arrangements. But soon enough the song transforms into a punishing slab of walloping, blasting drums and breakneck speed picking. It also boasts a very catchy and rhythmic, galloping beat, and a solo that is quite possibly the finest you will find anywhere on here. (It is a wailing, vertigo-inducing solo that just builds and builds...then it builds some more, thus helping to ensure that \\"The Day...\\" has an undeniable epic vibe to it.)<br /><br />\\"All Nightmare Long\\" opens with a nice bit of calming guitar melodies. No worries, though, because gobs of excellent, smoking, nimble-fingered buzzsaw riffing -- anchored by a stomping, thundering rhythm section -- abound soon thereafter. But this tune is more than just a throwback to Metallica's olden days, and it is different than the rest of the album. Much different, in fact. See, it features some astonishingly complex and technical time signatures, including plenty of \\"math-y\\" stops and starts, and fast tempo changes. Back on more traditional ground, \\"Cyanide\\" is \\"Death Magnetic\\"'s hit lead single. It features good bass work -- i.e. a Motorhead-esque bass intro and a steady, and kind of funky-sounding bass bottom -- throughout. And it doesn't stop there, either, because it is also home to another excellent guitar solo, some catchy, bouncy rhythms, and one of the best and most infectious choruses in Metallica's playbook.<br /><br />Unfortunately, what comes next is the record's sole stinker. Yes, \\"The Unforgiven III\\" might have a nicely somber piano intro and James' trademark crooning. But for the most part, this meandering, self-indulgent, and just plain boring ballad goes nowhere, adds nothing, and fails to stick with the listener for very long after hearing it. It is overlong, too. But whatever \\"The Unforgiven III\\" lacks in punch, \\"The Judas Kiss\\" makes up for and then some. It is an exhilarating barrage of blazing tempos and brutal balls of scorching, ripping modern thrash riffage and machine-gun-fast double bass drumming. Kirk does his part in making it a really memorable and air-guitar-able piece with both the above-described riff work and another epic, lengthy, wah-wah-inflected solo. And James' Judas Priest-y singing, triumphant, sing/shout along-worthy choruses, and noteworthy lyrics (which are very dark and cryptic) complete the song.<br /><br />\\"Suicide & Redemption\\" is a brilliantly-written, epic, expansive, and meticulous instrumental song that falls just short of being ten whole minutes long. It might not exactly be, say, \\"Orion,\\" but it is the first instrumental Metallica have recorded since their \\"...And Justice For All Days.\\" It is a terrifically hard-driving and hard-rocking cut that stitches together thrashy and blood-pumping tempos with ominously slower, and at times almost sludgy, Alice In Chains-worthy riffs. However, the set concludes with \\"My Apocalypse,\\" a totally straightforward, heads down riff-fest from start to finish. It just oozes with chunky, blustery, and sometimes even Slayer-worthy speed picking. Of course, the riffage wouldn't be quite as effective, here, if it weren't complimented well by crunching bass lines, pounding drums, and power metal-lite, fun-loving vocals.<br /><br />True, this might be the kind of album that you are just dying to hate. (If you listen closely enough, you might be able to hear some critics sharpening their knives before listening to it.) But it is also, simultaneously, an impossible album to hate. After all, \\"Death Magnetic\\" is a rewarding, satiating new millennium thrasherpiece, and a glorious return to studded form for James and the Gang. And it forgives any and all of the band's wrongdoings in the past (except for maybe the whole Napster debacle), and resoundingly answers any lingering questions that you might have about the band. (Yes, they are still relevant, inspired, and brutal as ever.) So just buy it, dang you, buy it, because trust me, folks, this record is one for the ages!The Day...\\" has an undeniable epic vibe to it.)<br /><br />\\"All Nightmare Long\\" opens with a nice bit of calming guitar melodies. B009AOFNU4|5.0|I develop game software for Android and have a sizable collection of wired and wireless gaming controllers. Unfortunately I need to buy each new controller to make sure it's compatible with my software. I purchased the SSF when it first became available and paid $90 for it ($80 + $10 shipping). To communicate with the bluetooth controllers, instead of linking in each company's SDK or helper app, I prefer to reverse engineer the bluetooth protocol and communicate directly with the device. Luckily the SSF supports both HID mode (normal gamepad input on PC's and Android) and a direct connect SPP mode (RFCOMM). Some have complained that the SSF is too small, but for me it's the perfect balance of size and comfort. One of the best features of the SSF is the analog controls. They self-center, require no calibration and work smoothly in all directions. The same cannot be said for competing controllers. The Nyko Playpad and PowerA MOGA both have stiff and uneven analog controls which don't give consistent values throughout their range (-128 to +127). To sum up:<br /><br />Pros:<br />1) Solidly built and comfortable in the hand.<br />2) Excellent bluetooth communication which supports HID joystick and RFCOMM modes<br />3) Long battery life<br />4) The best analog nubs of any wireless bluetooth controller<br />5) Small, but comfortable - easy to carry with you.<br /><br />Cons:<br />1) Price - $80 is too much for a gamepad<br />2) Included soft case prevents dust, but doesn't protect it. A hard case would be better.
